Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that all evil is merely the absence of good (non-existence).
Correction: Al-Razi shows that evil in actions (like inflicting pain) is an existential reality, not just absence of good.

Checkpoint
According to al-Razi's answer, what is the meaning of evil in actions?
A) Absence of a good attribute.
B) Inflicting pain (īlām).
C) Loss of life.
D) Fear of harm.

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi distinguishes evil in essence/attributes (non-existential) from evil in actions (existential pain), rebutting the claim that evil is only non-existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you suffer a painful event, do you tend to philosophize it away as 'merely the absence of good,' or do you confront it as a real, existent trial from Allah? How does Al-Razi's insistence that evil in actions is existential change the way you should respond to your own pain? Will you now allow your pain to drive you to sincere du'a and repentance rather than intellectual dismissal?
?
Think of a sin you committed—an action of injustice or harm. Have you ever excused it as 'just a lack of good' in the moment, rather than acknowledging it as an existent, blameworthy act? Al-Razi teaches that evil in actions is real and existential. How does that truth hold you accountable for even the 'small' sins you commit? Are you willing to repent from them with the same seriousness as if they were physical pain?
?
Al-Razi says that 'the meaning of intelligent people concerning evil... is the occurrence of pain and grief.' Are you intellectually honest about the pain you cause others? Is there someone you have hurt whose pain you have dismissed as 'not that bad' or 'just their perception'? How does this lesson demand that you re-evaluate your actions and seek to repair the existential harm you have inflicted?

Allah's Existence
intermediate
6 min
The Three Reasons Evil Does Not Deny Divine Wisdom
Author distinguishes evil types and gives three reasons for divine wisdom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three rational arguments that demonstrate why the existence of pain and pleasure in this world does not contradict God's wisdom.

Core Idea
Pain outweighs pleasure, yet existence itself is not evil; pleasure is merely the removal of pain.

The author now answers a key objection: if God is wise and good, why does He create a world filled with more pain than pleasure? He provides three distinct reasons, grounded in empirical observation and logical reasoning, to show that the presence of pain does not undermine divine wisdom. This lesson walks through those reasons.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish evil types
Read the opening line where the author distinguishes between evil in essence/attributes (non-existent) and evil in actions (existing). Understand that evil in actions is the focus.
This sets the scope of the argument.
2
First reason: pleasures vs pains
Examine the claim that pleasures are much weaker than pains, using examples like eating vs colic. Note the empirical basis.
Experience shows pain outweighs pleasure.
3
Second and third reasons
Study the second reason: non-existence avoids pain, so safety from pain is better. Then the third: pleasure is merely repelling pain (e.g., eating removes hunger).
These reasons show pain does not negate wisdom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في الذات والصفات . أمر عدمي . وأما في الأفعال : فلا شبهة أن الشر فيها معنى موجود وأما السؤال الثاني : فالجواب عنه من وجوه : الأول : أن لذات هذا العالم ، أضعف بكثير من ألم هذا العالم . والتجربة تدل عليه . فإن ألذ الأشياء : قضاء شهوة البطن ، وشهوة الفرج ونحن نعلم بالضرورة : أن ألم القولنج ، وسائر الأمراض الكثيرة أصعب بكثير من لذة الأكل والوقاع . والثاني : إن عند البقاء على العدم، لا يحصل ، لا اللذة ولا الألم وعند الوجود يحصل أنواع الآلام ، ولا شك أن السلامة من الألم ، أفضل من الوقوع في الألم . والثالث : أن ما يتوهم لذة في هذا العالم ، فهو في الحقيقة عبارة عن دفع الألم. فإن لذة الأكل عبارة عن دفع ألم الجوع، لذلك فكلما كان الجوع أقوى ، كان الأكل ألذ وقال بعض من يتمسك بأمثال هذه الكلمات إنه تعالى خلق القاتل والمقتول ، والظالم والمظلوم ، وعلم أن هذا يقتل ذلك الآخر ، ثم توعد القاتل بأن قال : متى قتلت ذلك الآخر : عذبتك بالنار . فلو لم يخلقهما ، لكان قد سلم المقتول من عذاب الدنيا ، والقاتل من عذاب الآخرة . فيثبت : أن الخلق فتح لباب الشر والآفات . وذلك لا يليق بالصانع الحكيم . وأما إثبات أن إله العالم مؤذي ، وليس بحكيم ولا رحيم ، ولا ناظر لعباده ، محسن إليهم. فذلك باطل ، بإجماع العقلاء المعتبرين . فلم يبق إلا أن يقال : مبدأ وجود العالم : آنية موجبة بالذات ، والماهية لوجود العالم . وذلك يوجب دوام العالم ، بدوام وجوده والله أعلم
In the essence and attributes, it is a non-existent matter. As for actions: there is no doubt that evil in them is an existing meaning. As for the second question: the answer to it is from several aspects: First: that the pleasures of this world are much weaker than the pain of this world. And experience indicates it. For the most pleasurable things: satisfying the appetite of the belly and the appetite of the private part, and we know necessarily that the pain of colic and the rest of the many diseases are much more severe than the pleasure of eating and intercourse. Second: that upon remaining in non-existence, neither pleasure nor pain occurs; and upon existence, types of pains occur; and there is no doubt that safety from pain is better than falling into pain. Third: that whatever is imagined as pleasure in this world is in reality an expression of repelling pain. For the pleasure of eating is an expression of repelling the pain of hunger; therefore, whenever hunger is stronger, the eating is more pleasurable. And some of those who adhere to such words said that He, exalted, created the killer and the killed, the oppressor and the oppressed, and knew that this one would kill that other, then threatened the killer by saying: When you kill that other, I will punish you with fire. So if He had not created them, the killed would have been saved from the punishment of this world, and the killer from the punishment of the Hereafter. So it is established that creation opened the door to evil and afflictions. And that is not befitting the Wise Maker. And as for proving that the God of the world is harmful, and not wise nor merciful, nor caring for His servants, beneficent to them — that is false by consensus of the rational considered ones. So nothing remains except to say: the origin of the existence of the world is a self-necessitating quiddity, and the quiddity for the existence of the world. And that necessitates the perpetuity of the world, with the perpetuity of its existence. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage is a response to an objection about the existence of evil in the world. The author first distinguishes between evil in essence/attributes (which is non-existent) and evil in actions (which exists). Then he answers a second question with three aspects: (1) Pleasures are weaker than pains, as known from experience; (2) Non-existence involves no pain, whereas existence involves many pains, so safety from pain is preferable; (3) Pleasures are merely the removal of pain (e.g., eating removes hunger), so there is no pure pleasure. Next, he refutes a further objection: if God creates a killer and a victim, He could have prevented both from suffering by not creating them. The author replies that this implies God is harmful and not merciful, which is false by rational consensus. Therefore, the only tenable conclusion is that the world originates from a necessary cause, implying its eternity. The author here is defending God's wisdom against the problem of evil by showing that creation involves more pain than pleasure, but this is not a defect; rather, it proves God's wisdom as the source of existence.

Key Terms
شر
ألم
لذة
دفع الألم
عدم
وجود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Pleasure is a positive, independent reality that outweighs pain in this world.
Correction: The author argues that pleasures are weaker than pains, and even pleasures are just the removal of pain, so they do not outweigh the pains experienced.

Checkpoint
According to the third aspect, what is the pleasure of eating?
A) A positive sensation added by God.
B) The removal of the pain of hunger.
C) An illusion with no basis.
D) A reward for good deeds.

Key Takeaway
The three reasons show that the presence of pain does not contradict divine wisdom; rather, they highlight that pleasure is derivative and pain is a test of existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you chase after worldly pleasures—like food, comfort, or entertainment—do you admit to yourself that you are actually just trying to escape pain? How does that shift your responsibility for your own desires?
?
If the greatest pleasures of this world are far weaker than its worst pains, why do you still invest so much energy in maximizing pleasure and avoiding pain? What does that reveal about your trust in God's wisdom?
?
You have experienced both pleasure and pain. Now that you know pleasure is merely the removal of pain, how will you train yourself to seek the lasting pleasure of the afterlife rather than the temporary relief of this world? What one concrete change will you make today?
